class="row first">\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h1>\n      Why AngularJS?\n     </h1>\n     <p>\n      HTML is great for declaring static documents, but it falters when we try to use it for\n          declaring dynamic views in web-applications. AngularJS lets you extend HTML vocabulary\n          for your application. The resulting environment is extraordinarily expressive, readable,\n          and quick to develop.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h1>\n      Alternatives\n     </h1>\n     <p>\n      Other frameworks deal with HTML\xe2\x80\x99s shortcomings by either abstracting away HTML, CSS,\n          and/or JavaScript or by providing an imperative way for manipulating the DOM. Neither of\n          these address the root problem that HTML was not designed for dynamic views.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h1>\n      Extensibility\n     </h1>\n     <p>\n      AngularJS is a toolset for building the framework most suited to your application\n          development. It is fully extensible and works well with other libraries. Every feature\n          can be modified or replaced to suit your unique development workflow and feature needs.\n          Read on to find out how.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <h1>\n    The Basics\n   </h1>\n   <div class="row example">\n    <div annotate="hello.annotation" app-source="hello.html" class="span8 app-source" style="clear: both;">\n     <div class="tabbable">\n      <ul class="nav nav-tabs">\n       <li class=" active">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#hello-html">\n         index.html\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <div class="tab-content">\n       <div class="tab-pane active" id="hello-html">\n        <pre class="prettyprint linenums nocode"><ol class="linenums"><li class="L0"><span class="dec">&lt;!doctype html&gt;</span></li><li class="L1"><span class="tag">&lt;html</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn"><code class="nocode" data-content="Tells AngularJS to be active in this portion of the page. In this case the entire document." data-original-title="&lt;code&gt;ng-app&lt;/code&gt;" rel="popover" style="background-color: rgb(153, 194, 255);">ng-app</code></span><span class="tag">&gt;</span></li><li class="L2"><span class="pln">  </span><span class="tag">&lt;head&gt;</span></li><li class="L3"><span class="pln">    </span><span class="tag">&lt;script</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">src</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"http://code.angularjs.org/<code class="nocode" data-content="Load AngularJS." data-original-title="&lt;code&gt;angular-1.0.0rc4.min.js&lt;/code&gt;" rel="popover" style="background-color: rgb(153, 194, 255);">angular-1.0.0rc4.min.js</code>"</span><span class="tag">&gt;&lt;/script&gt;</span></li><li class="L4"><span class="pln">  </span><span class="tag">&lt;/head&gt;</span></li><li class="L5"><span class="pln">  </span><span class="tag">&lt;body&gt;</span></li><li class="L6"><span class="pln">    </span><span class="tag">&lt;div&gt;</span></li><li class="L7"><span class="pln">      </span><span class="tag">&lt;label&gt;</span><span class="pln">Name:</span><span class="tag">&lt;/label&gt;</span></li><li class="L8"><span class="pln">      </span><span class="tag">&lt;input</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">type</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"text"</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn"><code class="nocode" data-content="This links the form and the model. This means that any changes to the control update the data in your model, and when you change the model it updates the control. Try it! Type in the control and see it update below." data-original-title="&lt;code&gt;ng-model&lt;/code&gt;" rel="popover" style="background-color: rgb(153, 194, 255);">ng-model</code></span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"yourName"</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">placeholder</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"Enter a name here"</span><span class="tag">&gt;</span></li><li class="L9"><span class="pln">      </span><span class="tag">&lt;hr&gt;</span></li><li class="L0"><span class="pln">      </span><span class="tag">&lt;h1&gt;</span><span class="pln">Hello <code class="nocode" data-content="The &lt;code&gt;{{ }}&lt;/code&gt; are a declarative way of specifying data binding locations in the HTML. AngularJS will automatically update this text whenever the &lt;code&gt;yourName&lt;/code&gt; property changes." data-original-title="&lt;code&gt;{{yourName}}&lt;/code&gt;" rel="popover" style="background-color: rgb(153, 194, 255);">{{yourName}}</code>!</span><span class="tag">&lt;/h1&gt;</span></li><li class="L1"><span class="pln">    </span><span class="tag">&lt;/div&gt;</span></li><li class="L2"><span class="pln">  </span><span class="tag">&lt;/body&gt;</span></li><li class="L3"><span class="tag">&lt;/html&gt;</span></li></ol></pre>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n     </div>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <span hint="">\n      <em>\n       Hint:\n      </em>\n      hover over\n      <code class="nocode" data-content="Place your mouse over highlited areas in the code for explanations." data-original-title="Hover" rel="popover" style="background-color: rgb(153, 194, 255);">\n       me\n      </code>\n      .\n     </span>\n     <span class="pull-right" js-fiddle="hello.html">\n      <form action="http://jsfiddle.net/api/post/library/pure/" class="jsfiddle" method="post" target="_blank">\n       <input name="title" type="hidden" value="AngularJS Example: "/>\n       <input name="css" type="hidden" value=\'&lt;/style&gt; &lt;!-- Ugly Hack due to jsFiddle issue: http://goo.gl/BUfGZ --&gt; \n&lt;link rel="stylesheet" href="http://twitter.github.com/bootstrap/assets/css/bootstrap.css"&gt;\n&lt;script src="http://code.angularjs.org/angular-1.0.0rc4.min.js"&gt;&lt;/script&gt;\n&lt;style&gt;\n\'/>\n       <input name="html" type="hidden" value=\'&lt;div ng-app&gt;\n  &lt;div&gt;\n    &lt;label&gt;Name:&lt;/label&gt;\n    &lt;input type="text" ng-model="yourName" placeholder="Enter a name here"&gt;\n    &lt;hr&gt;\n    &lt;h1&gt;Hello {{yourName}}!&lt;/h1&gt;\n  &lt;/div&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;\n\'/>\n       <input name="js" type="hidden" value=""/>\n       <button class="btn btn-primary">\n        <i class="icon-white icon-pencil">\n        </i>\n        Edit Me\n       </button>\n      </form>\n     </span>\n     <div class="tabs-spacer">\n     </div>\n     <div app-run="hello.html" class="well ng-scope">\n      <div>\n       <label>\n        Name:\n       </label>\n       <input class="ng-pristine ng-valid" ng-model="yourName" placeholder="Enter a name here" type="text"/>\n       <hr/>\n       <h1 class="ng-binding">\n        Hello !\n       </h1>\n      </div>\n     </div>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <h1>\n    Add Some Control\n   </h1>\n   <div class="row">\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Data Binding\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      Data-binding is an automatic way of updating the view whenever the model changes, as\n          well as updating the model whenever the view changes. This is awesome because it\n          eliminates DOM manipulation from the list of things you have to worry about.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Controller\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      Controllers are the behavior behind the DOM elements. AngularJS lets you express the\n          behavior in a clean readable form without usual boilerplate of updating the DOM,\n          registering callbacks or watching model changes.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Plain JavaScript\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      Unlike other frameworks, there is no need to inherit from proprietary types; to wrap the\n          model in accessors methods. Just plain old JavaScript here. This makes your code easy to\n          test, maintain, reuse, and again free from boilerplate.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <div class=" row example">\n    <div annotate="todo.annotation" app-source="todo.html todo.js todo.css" class="span8 app-source" style="clear: both;">\n     <div class="tabbable">\n      <ul class="nav nav-tabs">\n       <li class=" active">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#todo-html">\n         index.html\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li class="">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#todo-js">\n         todo.js\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li class="">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#todo-css">\n         todo.css\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <div class="tab-content">\n       <div class="tab-pane active" id="todo-html">\n        <pre class="prettyprint linenums nocode"><ol class="linenums"><li class="L0"><span class="dec">&lt;!doctype html&gt;</span></li><li class="L1"><span class="tag">&lt;html</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn"><code class="nocode" data-content="Tells AngularJS to be active in this portion of the page. function() {\n    $scope.todos.push({text:$scope.todoText, done:false});\n    $scope.todoText = \'\';\n  };\n\n  $scope.remaining = function() {\n    var count = 0;\n    angular.forEach($scope.todos, function(todo) {\n      count += todo.done ? 0 : 1;\n    });\n    return count;\n  };\n\n  $scope.archive = function() {\n    var oldTodos = $scope.todos;\n    $scope.todos = [];\n    angular.forEach(oldTodos, function(todo) {\n      if (!todo.done) $scope.todos.push(todo);\n    });\n  };\n}\n\n"/>\n       <button class="btn btn-primary">\n        <i class="icon-white </div>\n    <div class="modal-body">\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <h1>\n    Wire up a Backend\n   </h1>\n   <div class="row">\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Deep Linking\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      A deep link reflects where the user is in the app, this is useful so users can bookmark\n          and email links to locations within apps. Round trip apps get this automatically, but\n          AJAX apps by their nature do not. AngularJS combines the benefits of deep link with\n          desktop app-like behavior.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Form Validation\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      Client-side form validation is an important part of great user experience.\n          AngularJS lets you declare the validation rules of the form without having to write\n          JavaScript code. Write less code, go have beer sooner.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Server Communication\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      AngularJS provides services on top of XHR, that dramatically simplify your code. We wrap\n          XHR to give you exception management and promises. Promises further simplify your code\n          by handling asynchronous return of data. This lets you assign properties synchronously\n          when the return is actually asynchronous.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <div class=" row example">\n    <div annotate="project.annotation" app-source="project.html project.js list.html detail.html mongolab.js" class="span8 app-source" module="project" resource="resource" style="clear: both;">\n     <div class="tabbable">\n      <ul class="nav nav-tabs">\n       <li class=" active">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#project-html">\n         index.html\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li class="">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#project-js">\n         project.js\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li class="">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#list-html">\n         list.html\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li class="">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#detail-html">\n         detail.html\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li class="">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#mongolab-js">\n         mongolab.js\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <div class="tab-content">\n       <div class="tab-pane active" id="project-html">\n        <pre class="prettyprint linenums nocode"><ol class="linenums"><li class="L0"><span class="dec">&lt;!doctype html&gt;</span></li><li class="L1"><span class="tag">&lt;html</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn"><code class="nocode" data-content="Tells AngularJS to be active in this portion of the page.    </div>\n   </div>\n   <h1>\n    Create Components\n   </h1>\n   <div class="row">\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Directives\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      Directives is a unique and powerful feature available only in Angular. Directives let\n          you invent new HTML syntax, specific to your application.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Reusable Components\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      We use directives to create reusable components. A component allows you to hide complex\n          DOM structure, CSS, and behavior. This lets you focus either on what the application\n          does or how the application looks separately.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Localization\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      An important part of serious apps is localization. Angular\'s local aware filters and\n          stemming directives give you building blocks to make your application available in all\n          locales.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <div class=" row example">\n    <div annotate="tabs.annotation" app-source="tabs.html components.js beers.js" class="span8 app-source" module="components" style="clear: both;">\n     <div class="tabbable">\n      <ul class="nav nav-tabs">\n       <li class=" active">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#tabs-html">\n         index.html\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li class="">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#components-js">\n         components.js\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li class="">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#beers-js">\n         beers.js\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <div class="tab-content">\n       <div class="tab-pane active" id="tabs-html">\n        <pre class="prettyprint linenums nocode"><ol class="linenums"><li class="L0"><span class="dec">&lt;!doctype html&gt;</span></li><li class="L1"><span class="tag">&lt;html</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">ng-app</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"<code class="nocode" data-content="The &lt;code&gt;ng-app&lt;/code&gt; activates the &lt;code&gt;component&lt;/code&gt; module for this page region. <h3>\n      Embeddable\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      AngularJS works great with other technologies. Add as much or as little of AngularJSJS to\n          an existing page as you like. Many other frameworks require full commitment. This page\n          has multiple AngularJS applications embedded in it. Because AngularJS has no global\n          state multiple apps can run on a single page without the use of\n      <code>\n       iframe\n      </code>\n      s. We\n          encourage you to view-source and look around.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Injectable\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      The dependency injection in AngularJS allows you to declaratively describe how your\n          application is wired. This means that your your application needs no\n      <code>\n       main()\n      </code>\n      method which is usually an unmaintainable mess. Dependency injection is also a core to\n          AngularJS. This means that any component which does not fit your needs can easily be\n          replaced.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Testable\n     </h3>\n     AngularJS was designed from ground up to be testable. It encourages behavior-view\n          separation, comes pre-bundled with mocks, and takes full advantage of dependency\n          injection. It also comes with end-to-end scenario runner which eliminates test flakiness\n          by understanding the inner workings of AngularJS.\n     <p>\n     </p>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <hr/>\n  </div>\n  <footer class="footer">\n   <div class="container">\n    <p class="pull-right">\n     <a href="#">\n      Back to top\n     </a>\n    </p>\n    <p>\n     Super-powered by Google  \xc2\xa92010-2012\n    </p>\n    <p>\n     Code licensed under the\n     <a href="https://github.com/angular/angular.js/blob/master/LICENSE" target="_blank">\n      The\n          MIT License\n     </a>\n     . Here, for every object in &lt;code&gt;todos&lt;/code&gt;, AngularJS will create new copy of the &lt;code&gt;&amp;lt;li&amp;gt;&lt;/code&gt; element. Calling it updates the model, which then updates the view through data-binding. The &lt;code&gt;ng&amp;ndash;repeat&lt;/code&gt; is bound to this array. It automatically unrolls the array and adds the new DOM element into the view. (see &lt;code&gt;ng&amp;ndash;repeat&lt;/code&gt; in &lt;code&gt;index.html&lt;/code&gt; tab.)"\n        , "todoText": "Because of  bi-directional data-binding, the model is always up to date. class="row first">\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h1>\n      Why AngularJS?\n     </h1>\n     <p>\n      HTML is great for declaring static documents, but it falters when we try to use it for\n          declaring dynamic views in web-applications. AngularJS lets you extend HTML vocabulary\n          for your application. The resulting environment is extraordinarily expressive, readable,\n          and quick to develop.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h1>\n      Alternatives\n     </h1>\n     <p>\n      Other frameworks deal with HTML\xe2\x80\x99s shortcomings by either abstracting away HTML, CSS,\n          and/or JavaScript or by providing an imperative way for manipulating the DOM. Neither of\n          these address the root problem that HTML was not designed for dynamic views.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h1>\n      Extensibility\n     </h1>\n     <p>\n      AngularJS is a toolset for building the framework most suited to your application\n          development. It is fully extensible and works well with other libraries. Every feature\n          can be modified or replaced to suit your unique development workflow and feature needs.\n          Read on to find out how.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <h1>\n    The Basics\n   </h1>\n   <div class="row example">\n    <div annotate="hello.annotation" app-source="hello.html" class="span8 app-source" style="clear: both;">\n     <div class="tabbable">\n      <ul class="nav nav-tabs">\n       <li class=" active">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#hello-html">\n         index.html\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <div class="tab-content">\n       <div class="tab-pane active" id="hello-html">\n        <pre class="prettyprint linenums nocode"><ol class="linenums"><li class="L0"><span class="dec">&lt;!doctype html&gt;</span></li><li class="L1"><span class="tag">&lt;html</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn"><code class="nocode" data-content="Tells AngularJS to be active in this portion of the page. In this case the entire document." data-original-title="&lt;code&gt;ng-app&lt;/code&gt;" rel="popover" style="background-color: rgb(153, 194, 255);">ng-app</code></span><span class="tag">&gt;</span></li><li class="L2"><span class="pln">  </span><span class="tag">&lt;head&gt;</span></li><li class="L3"><span class="pln">    </span><span class="tag">&lt;script</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">src</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"http://code.angularjs.org/<code class="nocode" data-content="Load AngularJS." data-original-title="&lt;code&gt;angular-1.0.0rc4.min.js&lt;/code&gt;" rel="popover" style="background-color: rgb(153, 194, 255);">angular-1.0.0rc4.min.js</code>"</span><span class="tag">&gt;&lt;/script&gt;</span></li><li class="L4"><span class="pln">  </span><span class="tag">&lt;/head&gt;</span></li><li class="L5"><span class="pln">  </span><span class="tag">&lt;body&gt;</span></li><li class="L6"><span class="pln">    </span><span class="tag">&lt;div&gt;</span></li><li class="L7"><span class="pln">      </span><span class="tag">&lt;label&gt;</span><span class="pln">Name:</span><span class="tag">&lt;/label&gt;</span></li><li class="L8"><span class="pln">      </span><span class="tag">&lt;input</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">type</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"text"</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn"><code class="nocode" data-content="This links the form and the model. This means that any changes to the control update the data in your model, and when you change the model it updates the control. Try it! Type in the control and see it update below." data-original-title="&lt;code&gt;ng-model&lt;/code&gt;" rel="popover" style="background-color: rgb(153, 194, 255);">ng-model</code></span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"yourName"</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">placeholder</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"Enter a name here"</span><span class="tag">&gt;</span></li><li class="L9"><span class="pln">      </span><span class="tag">&lt;hr&gt;</span></li><li class="L0"><span class="pln">      </span><span class="tag">&lt;h1&gt;</span><span class="pln">Hello <code class="nocode" data-content="The &lt;code&gt;{{ }}&lt;/code&gt; are a declarative way of specifying data binding locations in the HTML. AngularJS will automatically update this text whenever the &lt;code&gt;yourName&lt;/code&gt; property changes." data-original-title="&lt;code&gt;{{yourName}}&lt;/code&gt;" rel="popover" style="background-color: rgb(153, 194, 255);">{{yourName}}</code>!</span><span class="tag">&lt;/h1&gt;</span></li><li class="L1"><span class="pln">    </span><span class="tag">&lt;/div&gt;</span></li><li class="L2"><span class="pln">  </span><span class="tag">&lt;/body&gt;</span></li><li class="L3"><span class="tag">&lt;/html&gt;</span></li></ol></pre>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n     </div>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <span hint="">\n      <em>\n       Hint:\n      </em>\n      hover over\n      <code class="nocode" data-content="Place your mouse over highlited areas in the code for explanations." data-original-title="Hover" rel="popover" style="background-color: rgb(153, 194, 255);">\n       me\n      </code>\n      .\n     </span>\n     <span class="pull-right" js-fiddle="hello.html">\n      <form action="http://jsfiddle.net/api/post/library/pure/" class="jsfiddle" method="post" target="_blank">\n       <input name="title" type="hidden" value="AngularJS Example: "/>\n       <input name="css" type="hidden" value=\'&lt;/style&gt; &lt;!-- Ugly Hack due to jsFiddle issue: http://goo.gl/BUfGZ --&gt; \n&lt;link rel="stylesheet" href="http://twitter.github.com/bootstrap/assets/css/bootstrap.css"&gt;\n&lt;script src="http://code.angularjs.org/angular-1.0.0rc4.min.js"&gt;&lt;/script&gt;\n&lt;style&gt;\n\'/>\n       <input name="html" type="hidden" value=\'&lt;div ng-app&gt;\n  &lt;div&gt;\n    &lt;label&gt;Name:&lt;/label&gt;\n    &lt;input type="text" ng-model="yourName" placeholder="Enter a name here"&gt;\n    &lt;hr&gt;\n    &lt;h1&gt;Hello {{yourName}}!&lt;/h1&gt;\n  &lt;/div&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;\n\'/>\n       <input name="js" type="hidden" value=""/>\n       <button class="btn btn-primary">\n        <i class="icon-white icon-pencil">\n        </i>\n        Edit Me\n       </button>\n      </form>\n     </span>\n     <div class="tabs-spacer">\n     </div>\n     <div app-run="hello.html" class="well ng-scope">\n      <div>\n       <label>\n        Name:\n       </label>\n       <input class="ng-pristine ng-valid" ng-model="yourName" placeholder="Enter a name here" type="text"/>\n       <hr/>\n       <h1 class="ng-binding">\n        Hello !\n       </h1>\n      </div>\n     </div>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <h1>\n    Add Some Control\n   </h1>\n   <div class="row">\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Data Binding\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      Data-binding is an automatic way of updating the view whenever the model changes, as\n          well as updating the model whenever the view changes. This is awesome because it\n          eliminates DOM manipulation from the list of things you have to worry about.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Controller\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      Controllers are the behavior behind the DOM elements. AngularJS lets you express the\n          behavior in a clean readable form without usual boilerplate of updating the DOM,\n          registering callbacks or watching model changes.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Plain JavaScript\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      Unlike other frameworks, there is no need to inherit from proprietary types; to wrap the\n          model in accessors methods. Just plain old JavaScript here. This makes your code easy to\n          test, maintain, reuse, and again free from boilerplate.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <div class=" row example">\n    <div annotate="todo.annotation" app-source="todo.html todo.js todo.css" class="span8 app-source" style="clear: both;">\n     <div class="tabbable">\n      <ul class="nav nav-tabs">\n       <li class=" active">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#todo-html">\n         index.html\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li class="">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#todo-js">\n         todo.js\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li class="">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#todo-css">\n         todo.css\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <div class="tab-content">\n       <div class="tab-pane active" id="todo-html">\n        <pre class="prettyprint linenums nocode"><ol class="linenums"><li class="L0"><span class="dec">&lt;!doctype html&gt;</span></li><li class="L1"><span class="tag">&lt;html</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn"><code class="nocode" data-content="Tells AngularJS to be active in this portion of the page. function() {\n    $scope.todos.push({text:$scope.todoText, done:false});\n    $scope.todoText = \'\';\n  };\n\n  $scope.remaining = function() {\n    var count = 0;\n    angular.forEach($scope.todos, function(todo) {\n      count += todo.done ? 0 : 1;\n    });\n    return count;\n  };\n\n  $scope.archive = function() {\n    var oldTodos = $scope.todos;\n    $scope.todos = [];\n    angular.forEach(oldTodos, function(todo) {\n      if (!todo.done) $scope.todos.push(todo);\n    });\n  };\n}\n\n"/>\n       <button class="btn btn-primary">\n        <i class="icon-white </div>\n    <div class="modal-body">\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <h1>\n    Wire up a Backend\n   </h1>\n   <div class="row">\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Deep Linking\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      A deep link reflects where the user is in the app, this is useful so users can bookmark\n          and email links to locations within apps. Round trip apps get this automatically, but\n          AJAX apps by their nature do not. AngularJS combines the benefits of deep link with\n          desktop app-like behavior.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Form Validation\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      Client-side form validation is an important part of great user experience.\n          AngularJS lets you declare the validation rules of the form without having to write\n          JavaScript code. Write less code, go have beer sooner.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Server Communication\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      AngularJS provides services on top of XHR, that dramatically simplify your code. We wrap\n          XHR to give you exception management and promises. Promises further simplify your code\n          by handling asynchronous return of data. This lets you assign properties synchronously\n          when the return is actually asynchronous.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <div class=" row example">\n    <div annotate="project.annotation" app-source="project.html project.js list.html detail.html mongolab.js" class="span8 app-source" module="project" resource="resource" style="clear: both;">\n     <div class="tabbable">\n      <ul class="nav nav-tabs">\n       <li class=" active">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#project-html">\n         index.html\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li class="">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#project-js">\n         project.js\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li class="">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#list-html">\n         list.html\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li class="">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#detail-html">\n         detail.html\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li class="">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#mongolab-js">\n         mongolab.js\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <div class="tab-content">\n       <div class="tab-pane active" id="project-html">\n        <pre class="prettyprint linenums nocode"><ol class="linenums"><li class="L0"><span class="dec">&lt;!doctype html&gt;</span></li><li class="L1"><span class="tag">&lt;html</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn"><code class="nocode" data-content="Tells AngularJS to be active in this portion of the page. <span class="ng-scope">\n       </span>\n      </div>\n     </div>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <h1>\n    Create Components\n   </h1>\n   <div class="row">\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Directives\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      Directives is a unique and powerful feature available only in Angular. Directives let\n          you invent new HTML syntax, specific to your application.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Reusable Components\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      We use directives to create reusable components. A component allows you to hide complex\n          DOM structure, CSS, and behavior. This lets you focus either on what the application\n          does or how the application looks separately.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Localization\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      An important part of serious apps is localization. Angular\'s local aware filters and\n          stemming directives give you building blocks to make your application available in all\n          locales.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <div class=" row example">\n    <div annotate="tabs.annotation" app-source="tabs.html components.js beers.js" class="span8 app-source" module="components" style="clear: both;">\n     <div class="tabbable">\n      <ul class="nav nav-tabs">\n       <li class=" active">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#tabs-html">\n         index.html\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li class="">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#components-js">\n         components.js\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li class="">\n        <a data-toggle="tab" href="#beers-js">\n         beers.js\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <div class="tab-content">\n       <div class="tab-pane active" id="tabs-html">\n        <pre class="prettyprint linenums nocode"><ol class="linenums"><li class="L0"><span class="dec">&lt;!doctype html&gt;</span></li><li class="L1"><span class="tag">&lt;html</span><span class="pln"> </span><span class="atn">ng-app</span><span class="pun">=</span><span class="atv">"<code class="nocode" data-content="The &lt;code&gt;ng-app&lt;/code&gt; activates the &lt;code&gt;component&lt;/code&gt; module for this page region. <h3>\n      Embeddable\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      AngularJS works great with other technologies. Add as much or as little of AngularJSJS to\n          an existing page as you like. Many other frameworks require full commitment. This page\n          has multiple AngularJS applications embedded in it. Because AngularJS has no global\n          state multiple apps can run on a single page without the use of\n      <code>\n       iframe\n      </code>\n      s. We\n          encourage you to view-source and look around.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Injectable\n     </h3>\n     <p>\n      The dependency injection in AngularJS allows you to declaratively describe how your\n          application is wired. This means that your your application needs no\n      <code>\n       main()\n      </code>\n      method which is usually an unmaintainable mess. Dependency injection is also a core to\n          AngularJS. This means that any component which does not fit your needs can easily be\n          replaced.\n     </p>\n    </div>\n    <div class="span4">\n     <h3>\n      Testable\n     </h3>\n     AngularJS was designed from ground up to be testable. It encourages behavior-view\n          separation, comes pre-bundled with mocks, and takes full advantage of dependency\n          injection. It also comes with end-to-end scenario runner which eliminates test flakiness\n          by understanding the inner workings of AngularJS.\n     <p>\n     </p>\n    </div>\n   </div>\n   <hr/>\n  </div>\n  <footer class="footer">\n   <div class="container">\n    <p class="pull-right">\n     <a href="#">\n      Back to top\n     </a>\n    </p>\n    <p>\n     Super-powered by Google  \xc2\xa92010-2012\n    </p>\n    <p>\n     Code licensed under the\n     <a href="https://github.com/angular/angular.js/blob/master/LICENSE" target="_blank">\n      The\n          MIT License\n     </a>\n     .
